-------- Original Message --------
Subject: [micro-manager-general] New release: Micro-Manager 1.4.21
Date: 2015-05-01 03:02
 From: Mark Tsuchida <...>

Hi All,

We have just released Micro-Manager 1.4.21.
This is primarily a maintenance release with a lot of bug fixes. There
are also enhancements for various devices.

It can be downloaded (for Windows and Mac) from
http://micro-manager.org/wiki/Download_Micro-Manager_Latest_Release
where you can also view a list of changes since 1.4.20.

Thank you all for your contributions and feedback. It's what keeps
Micro-Manager going, so please keep it coming! If you find any issues
in version 1.4.21, please report them by starting a new thread on this
mailing list or sending a Problem Report (from Micro-Manager's Help
menu).

Unless special circumstances arise, our next release will be at the
end of July, 2015.

Best Regards,
The Micro-Manager Team

Subject: [OpenSPIM] very slow acquisition speed

Message-ID: <55477185.7040602@ist.ac.at>

Hi OpenSPIMists,

I have a plain vanilla OpenSpim that I set up > a year ago. Recently I 
noticed that the acquisition speed dropped to 1.5 frames/s. This is also 
the case when I am not moving the stage (single slice time lapse) and 
keeping the laser on continuously. I remember that was not a problem 
initially and that I got something like 10 frames/s in a z-stack which 
was good enough for me.
I can record with the full frame rate of the camera in micromanager so 
this doesn't seem to be the problem either.

I also tried the new 64bit version (which works fine btw.) but that did 
not change anything in terms of acquisition speed.

Any help is really appreciated!

Robert

Hi Monika,

On 2015-05-05 17:29, m.pawlowska at nencki.gov.pl wrote:
> W dniu 2015-05-05 14:03, Johannes Schindelin napisa?(a):
> 
>>> if I want to get OpenSPIM through fiji update site, I also need to
>>> activate the MicroManager-dev update site, or will it be installed
>>> automatically as a dependency of OpenSPIM?
>> 
>> It will be added automatically when you restart after activating the
>> OpenSPIM update site.
> 
> And what version of Micro-Manager will be downloaded? The last
> release, the nightly build, or something else?

The Micro-Manager-dev update site is populated automatically by the 
nightly build (read: by Micro-Manager's very own Jenkins job).

> I'm confused, because in the "About MicroManager" it says "MM Studio 
> version: 1.4.22 20150430, MMCore version 7.0.2" (I updated today) while 
> on the Micro-Manager website it says "Download Micro-Manager Latest 
> Release, Micro-Manager 1.4.21 (April 30, 2015) ". Yet the newest 
> nightly build is from May 4th.

Yeah, 1.4.22 is definitely wrong, most likely a typo (or preparing for 
the next release which is due July 31st).

The version you have as per the Micro-Manager-dev update site would be 
most appropriately described as 1.4.22-SNAPSHOT, i.e. a volatile version 
leading up to 1.4.22.

> I'm asking because I'm having issues with Micromanager, more precisely
> with Tools->Pixel Size Calibration, and I'm wondering whether going to
> an older or newer version would remove them.

The Micro-Manager developers are extremely helpful and nice, and they 
are very responsive (but keep in mind that they are in a different time 
zone: San Francisco, i.e. 9 hours behind us). I would suggest to write a 
mail to micro-manager-general at lists.sourceforge.net that describes the 
problem precisely -- ideally in such a manner that it is easy for any 
reader to reproduce the problem quickly. In my experience, most such bug 
descriptions on the mailing list are addressed swiftly.

Ciao,
Johannes

Hi All and especially Pete,

My setup is Orca R2, Coherent Cube, Picard stage.
I tested a couple of things and it it still unclear to me where the time 
is wasted.

I attached the core log of a 10 frame long time series (100ms exposure) 
recorded to memory with X/Y/Z Stage/Theta all unchecked and  without 
"Update Live preview".

I tried two configurations:
1. Orca  + Cube + Picard
2. Orca  + Picard

"1" took 7.6 s of which ("1"- "2") = 1.4 s are communication with laser, 
which, while way too much, is not the source of the problem.

Profiler("performAcquisition")[4 children]: 7.6113s
0.0017%:    Profiler("Output")[0 children]: 0.0001s
0.0000%:    Profiler("Acquisition")[0 children]: 0.0000s
24.0133%:    Profiler("Movement")[0 children]: 1.8277s
0.0013%:    Profiler("Setup")[0 children]: 0.0001s

So most of the time the system is doing something that the Profiler is 
not recording.

Looking at the core log I am a bit puzzled why the laser power is 
queried once  per slice and why the stage is told to move to the very 
position it currently is even though none of the motors should move at 
all since X/Y/Z/Theta are all unchecked in the acquisition dialog.

I would really appreciate any hint/suggestion on how to get back to 
reasonable acquisition speeds.

Thanks again!

Robert

> Hi All and especially Pete,
> 
> My setup is Orca R2, Coherent Cube, Picard stage.
> I tested a couple of things and it it still unclear to me where the 
> time
> is wasted.
> 
> I attached the core log of a 10 frame long time series (100ms exposure)
> recorded to memory with X/Y/Z Stage/Theta all unchecked and  without
> "Update Live preview".
> 
> I tried two configurations:
> 1. Orca  + Cube + Picard
> 2. Orca  + Picard
> 
> "1" took 7.6 s of which ("1"- "2") = 1.4 s are communication with 
> laser,
> which, while way too much, is not the source of the problem.
> 
> Profiler("performAcquisition")[4 children]: 7.6113s
> 0.0017%:    Profiler("Output")[0 children]: 0.0001s
> 0.0000%:    Profiler("Acquisition")[0 children]: 0.0000s
> 24.0133%:    Profiler("Movement")[0 children]: 1.8277s
> 0.0013%:    Profiler("Setup")[0 children]: 0.0001s
> 
> So most of the time the system is doing something that the Profiler is
> not recording.
> 
> Looking at the core log I am a bit puzzled why the laser power is
> queried once  per slice and why the stage is told to move to the very
> position it currently is even though none of the motors should move at
> all since X/Y/Z/Theta are all unchecked in the acquisition dialog.
> 
> I would really appreciate any hint/suggestion on how to get back to
> reasonable acquisition speeds.
> 
> Thanks again!
> 
> Robert

From johannes.schindelin at gmx.de  Fri May  8 05:31:24 2015
From: johannes.schindelin at gmx.de (Johannes Schindelin)
Date: Fri, 08 May 2015 12:31:24 +0200
Subject: [OpenSPIM] New Micro-Manager API: Home()
In-Reply-To: <d551ed95dc93c8e98d53d560336b288e@nencki.gov.pl>
References: <mailman.4303.1430923337.3596.openspim@openspim.org>
	<d551ed95dc93c8e98d53d560336b288e@nencki.gov.pl>
Message-ID: <93acf586b841b29c1d261c4d55bb95e8@www.dscho.org>

Hi Monika,

On 2015-05-07 19:11, m.pawlowska at nencki.gov.pl wrote:
> I tried to do it, just to see whether I can, but I can't and I feel
> that again the problem is not having sufficient information :/ How can
> I find out how this "SVN r15408" relates to the version available via
> Micro-Manager-Dev update site?

Unfortunately, it is not recorded. However, you can see the original 
Subversion revision (which the "SVN r15408" is referring to) in the 
commit message of our Git mirror, on the bottom of the commit messages. 
For example, r15408 corresponds to 
https://github.com/openspim/micromanager/commit/c46cd66d43e7fd55045ee690e281833dc0583d99 
which was committed on Tuesday, May 5th, so it should be in the nightly 
build as of Wednesday, May 6th (and as a consequence on the 
Micro-Manager-dev update site the same day, or at least one day later).

> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.194887 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Will home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.208887 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Did home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.208887 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Will home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.224888 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Did home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.224888 tid5692 [IFO,App] Could not home Z stage.
>                                    [       ] java.lang.Exception:
> Device "Picard Z Stage" is of the wrong type for the requested
> operation in Thread[AWT-EventQueue-0,6,main]

It appears that this error message comes from 
https://github.com/openspim/micromanager/blob/f88b6b5ff341061d777511e33c7291a3d498d431/MMCore/DeviceManager.h#L97 
(I called `git grep "of the wrong type"` to find out).

The commit you referenced replaced the `GetDeviceOfType()` call in 
`MMCore::home()` with a `GetDevice()` call: 
https://github.com/openspim/micromanager/commit/c46cd66d43e7fd55045ee690e281833dc0583d99#diff-66e4d1b12dce965612b0d94db6c9f1d6R1619 
-- therefore I think that this line:

>                                    [       ]   at
> mmcorej.MMCoreJJNI.CMMCore_home(Native Method)

hints at outdated Micro-Manager binaries. Having said that, it appears 
as if the Micro-Manager-dev update site has not been updated in a couple 
of days: http://sites.imagej.net/Micro-Manager-dev/mm/win64/?C=M;O=D

I have to run right now, but will investigate more later.

Thank you,
Johannes

From johannes.schindelin at gmx.de  Wed May 13 04:17:30 2015
From: johannes.schindelin at gmx.de (Johannes Schindelin)
Date: Wed, 13 May 2015 11:17:30 +0200
Subject: [OpenSPIM] very slow acquisition speed
In-Reply-To: <5551F4F5.3050403@ist.ac.at>
References: <mailman.4342.1431012438.3596.openspim@openspim.org>
	<b25a1860360928b2fc54bbc7721b4dde@nencki.gov.pl>
	<5551F4F5.3050403@ist.ac.at>
Message-ID: <a858dafc1c8aae2d5342914d10a57181@www.dscho.org>

Hi Robert,

On 2015-05-12 14:41, Robert Hauschild wrote:

> Would be great if someone could tell me how to figure out what is
> going on during the 75% of time that is unaccounted for in the
> profiler!

The profiler (which one are you using? That information is missing from 
the original report) can only profile Java code, not native code. So my 
guess is that something wonky is going on in the C++ part. 
Alternatively, it could be that the code is just waiting for the motors 
to arrive at the desired position, which would also not be recorded by 
the profiler.

Personally, I would try to go for the Flight Recorder of Java Mission 
Control: http://fiji.sc/Profiling_Java_Code#Java_Mission_Control. There 
is an Eclipse plugin with which you can toggle the flight recording more 
precisely; It is not described in the Fiji wiki because neither I nor 
anybody else found the time to describe it there, but there are links on 
Oracle's site: 
http://www.oracle.com/technetwork/java/javaseproducts/mission-control/index.html

Ciao,
Johannes

From johannes.schindelin at gmx.de  Wed May 13 04:59:00 2015

Subject: [OpenSPIM] 64-bit Fiji Memory Limit Issue
In-Reply-To: <1431353493456.12540@ucl.ac.uk>

	<90a6504ba069c146ee8efa3e28778233@www.dscho.org>

	<1431353493456.12540@ucl.ac.uk>
Message-ID: <a88c576f3ff07f4d01e577487451809b@www.dscho.org>

Dear Thomas,

please note that while it is convenient for you to take this problem to 
a private mail exchange with me, it is really inconvenient for me: I 
have nothing to gain from a private mail exchange solving this issue -- 
it is taking my time, to solve a problem that is not mine, in a plugin 
that is not mine, and the warm and fuzzy feeling of solving a single 
problem for a single person when nobody else knows what I managed to 
accomplish does not further my career nor does it pay my bills -- while 
a public discussion not only offers the possibility that other people 
than you might benefit from my advice (which would in turn help me), but 
also offers the possibility that other people might help you, relieving 
me.

I really wish that more people were trying to help the OpenSPIM 
community thrive as a publicly visible community. There are some 
laudable examples on the OpenSPIM mailing list recently, and I am very 
thankful for that.

On 2015-05-11 16:11, Roberts, Thomas wrote:

> I am still encountering this memory issue, unfortunately.
> 
> I downloaded the latest version of the OpenSPIM software that you sent
> a link to a few weeks ago
> (http://openspim.org/downloads/OpenSPIM-20150427.zip).

Please note that it is not obvious from your screenshots what amount of 
memory Fiji *actually* reserves. Two Fiji instances running side by 
side, for example, will not have the same amount of memory available 
because Java works by reserving the memory at start-up, and that memory 
is then not available to a second Fiji instance. The ImageJ launcher 
will detect that less memory is available than it was asked to ask for 
and fall back to try with a lesser amount. That is my guess regarding 
what happens on your computer.

By clicking on the status bar, you will see how much memory Fiji's Java 
VM thinks is available. Clicking on the status bar will also trigger a 
so-called "garbage collection", i.e. it will ask the Java VM to 
re-organize its memory consumption. Therefore, sporadically clicking on 
the status bar while the plugin is running might even work around the 
memory issue.

> However, I still can't open large images in Fiji. I am trying to run
> through the Bead Based Registration tutorial on OpenSPIM.org, but I
> encounter the Memory Limit issue - I've attached some PNGs showing the
> error messages.
> 
> I tried your suggestion of opening the memory monitor, but it doesn't
> really tell me much - just that the program spikes and stops once it
> reaches the 494MB memory limit (see image1.png).
> 
> I still don't understand why Fiji thinks it has 5000MB of memory
> available, but crashes at 500MB (see image2.png).

You really scared me when you said that it crashed. You see, "to crash" 
means one very specific thing, and that thing only, when you talk about 
computer programs: it means that the entire application just stopped to 
run, all its windows vanished, without any error message nor a chance to 
store so-far unsaved data.

That is distinctly not what happened. What you saw is an 
OutOfMemoryException which stopped the plugin but nothing else.

> Also, I have tried running the registration tutorial on my office
> computer, and this works, but the machine is very slow for such large
> datasets.

It might make sense to open large images in that Fiji instance first, 
until it runs out of memory, in order to determine whether the problem 
lies with the Java VM in general, or with the plugin you are trying to 
run. I am getting the impression that something is wrong with your Fiji 
installation rather than with the SPIM Registration plugin.

Ciao,
Johannes

any physical movement:

Hi Monika,

On Wed, May 13, 2015 at 09:38:21AM -0700, Chris Weisiger wrote:
> On Wed, May 13, 2015 at 9:15 AM, <m.pawlowska at nencki.gov.pl> wrote:
> > W dniu 2015-05-13 17:52, Chris Weisiger napisa?(a):
> > indeed, with the newest nightly build the acquisition works. But this
> > solves my problem only partly. I am normally using fiji with  
> Micromanager
> > update site, and from there the newest build is the 20150430, this is  
> why
> > I'm using this version. I would prefer to use fiji to have all the
> > aditional functionality. Is there any chance to get the update site
> > updated, so to say?
>
> Okay, good to know we've at least narrowed down what's going on. In this
> case I suspect the actual problem isn't the version of Micro-Manager, but
> the version of the OME library in Fiji. Sometimes Micro-Manager and Fiji
> depend on the same library, but require different versions of that  
> library,
> which is unfortunate; we're trying to resolve such issues when we  
> discover
> them.
>
> In the meantime, you can try replacing the library manually. This is a  
> jar
> file called "ome-xml.jar", which should be in the "plugins/Micro-Manager"
> directory of the nightly download. You can try just replacing the
> corresponding .jar file in your Fiji installation with the one from the
> nightly build. Make a backup of the original .jar file though, just in  
> case
> something else in Fiji breaks. In the meantime, we can look into what it
> would take to get the update site updated.

The conflict is in other JARs. We still use an outdated version of
scifio.jar, which conflicts with the newer version in Fiji. We fully
intend to fix this, and it will hopefully not be too hard, but it is not
trivial (we need to make sure we don't introduce issues into file saving
in our official release, and that will require careful testing).

Please consider the Micro-Manager-dev update site to be experimental.

I don't think there is an easy fix at this moment that can be done by
just replacing JARs. We'll keep working on it!

Best,
Mark

I have discovered a problem with micromanager 1.4.22 and the Orca ER. When I take a z-stack the resulting images are split. The left 1/3 of the image is fused to the right 2/3. The problem has something to to do with the Picard stage as taking 10 images quickly without stage movement results in intact images. Taking images of multiple xy positions results in split images. I replaced the Orca ER and associated control box with another Orca ER setup and the problem persisted.  I reinstalled an earlier version of micromanager (1.4.19) and the problem went away. Are earlier versions of Openspim software archived somewhere? I would like to download a version with mm 1.4.19.

Michael Redd

Hello Aryeh,

At the time we were using a Hamamatsu Orca ER, which is firewire based, hence the need for a computer with a firewire port. A portable laptop computer is a nice thing to have, but not necessary. 

Nowadays we cover many more models of camera, and I would personally suggest that you buy a sCMOS due to their larger field of view and improved speed.  

Best Regards,
Pete

> At the time we were using a Hamamatsu Orca ER, which is firewire based, hence the need for a computer with a firewire port. A portable laptop computer is a nice thing to have, but not necessary.
>
> Nowadays we cover many more models of camera, and I would personally suggest that you buy a sCMOS due to their larger field of view and improved speed.

Very good -- in this case we have many options, especially with USB3.0.

From fredrik.ek at med.lu.se  Tue May 26 01:24:52 2015
From: fredrik.ek at med.lu.se (Fredrik Ek)
Date: Tue, 26 May 2015 06:24:52 +0000
Subject: [OpenSPIM] multiline openSPIM with Lighthub-4
In-Reply-To: <55636591.6040901@cc.huji.ac.il>
References: <555AFFD5.9010106@cc.huji.ac.il>
	<180212231.32691920.1432027731107.JavaMail.zimbra@mpi-cbg.de>
	<555B0B70.9090300@cc.huji.ac.il> <55636591.6040901@cc.huji.ac.il>
Message-ID: <11FEABF97C42FE47AA23C843A13D49EEEDB2839A@UWMBX04.uw.lu.se>

Hi Aryeh,

We have just recently finished the build of a dual side illumination system using the lighthub-6 with 3 laser lines. I will upload pictures and details within next coming weeks on the wiki page. The first point is to go for the lighthub-6 since the price difference is very small. This will allow an expansion in the future with more lasers. The fiber is coupled to a fiber collimator fixed to a holder on a rail to allow for alignment with the beam splitter. Today I would have built it with a small xz stage for improved alignment or at least a sturdier holder of the collimator. There are some examples at Thorlabs. I have added the links to the details that we used in the current setup. It is important to get a good fixation of the collimator especially if you like to use the laser module in other microscopes and regularly shifts the fiber. 

I hope this will help you!

collimator http://www.thorlabs.de/thorproduct.cfm?partnumber=F240APC-A
adaptor http://www.thorlabs.de/thorproduct.cfm?partnumber=AD12NT
Holder http://www.thorlabs.de/thorproduct.cfm?partnumber=FMP1

BR

Fredrik

From winfrees at iu.edu  Tue May 26 11:04:41 2015
From: winfrees at iu.edu (Winfree, Seth)
Date: Tue, 26 May 2015 16:04:41 +0000
Subject: [OpenSPIM] perfusion and multiple lasers
Message-ID: <0BB84AC4E46D2D4AB1AE4C111324E8D63E390C96@IU-MSSG-MBX107.ads.iu.edu>

SPIMers,

We have completed a multichannel AOTF modulated 4 line L-SPIM.  We took an AOTF and three retired lasers(442,488,514,568,647) from our spinning disk and designed a DAC based on the Arduino DAC supported by micromanager (the 442 is not quite integrated optically).  We've also incorporated an emission filter wheel and excitation wheel for beam characterizing (the former is integrated in our branch of the SPIMAcquisition plugin).  I plan to have the optics/hardware/software design and example datasets up on the OpenSPIM site in the coming weeks-grant taking precedent.  I'm working with Johannes to get our branch of SPIMAcquisition merged with the release version-waiting on me really.

On the perfusion and environmental control side, we have a summer student that is working on these aspects for our system.  The perfusion is going to be fairly rudimentary.  We will be relying on peristaltic pumps because the volume of our sample chamber is so large (7 ml).  The perfusion system will be setup to work as a recirculating loop as well to deliver dissolved gases CO2 etc as required-via a simple bubbler.  If I can find a CO2 sensor I like(cost to performance) this might be integrated into the bubbler unit.

I'm not crazy about directly heating the chamber with amped up resistors, so we're starting with a "closed-loop" heated reservoir, re-circulator and heat-exchanger-if it works well we may also strap a Peltier based heat pump to the reservoir as well to give us cooling.

In toto there will be a handful of peristaltic pumps, controllers (Arduino as PIDs), media bubblers and heated reservoirs.  As time permits we'll be writing a plugin for micromanager to wrangle all this functionality and add graphs etc-everything you might want out of a comparable Peco or Okolabs solution.

As we make progress I'll update our  to-be-completed OpenSPIM page.
Happy SPIMing!

Seth

From weber at mpi-cbg.de  Wed May 27 10:41:22 2015
From: weber at mpi-cbg.de (Michael Weber)
Date: Wed, 27 May 2015 17:41:22 +0200
Subject: [OpenSPIM] sCMOS global vs rolling shutter
In-Reply-To: <5564744D.4000408@cc.huji.ac.il>
References: <555AFFD5.9010106@cc.huji.ac.il>	<180212231.32691920.1432027731107.JavaMail.zimbra@mpi-cbg.de>	<555B0B70.9090300@cc.huji.ac.il>
	<55636591.6040901@cc.huji.ac.il>
	<11FEABF97C42FE47AA23C843A13D49EEEDB2839A@UWMBX04.uw.lu.se>
	<5564744D.4000408@cc.huji.ac.il>
Message-ID: <BA71BC0A-3573-4ACB-9F0B-235CF40EBA13@mpi-cbg.de>

Dear Aryeh,

rolling shutter gives you twice the speed, but potential artifacts caused by the time offset across the frame. There are cameras which give you both shutter modes (Andor Zyla etc.), if you are willing to give up some QE. It really depends on your specimen, and what kind of analysis you want to do. Unless you want to quantify rapid movements across the frame (e.g. fast fluidics), I would say rolling shutter is fine.

Best,
Michael

On May 26, 2015, at 3:25 PM, Aryeh Weiss <aryeh at CC.HUJI.AC.IL> wrote:

I have a plain vanilla OpenSpim that I set up > a year ago. Recently I

initially and that I got something like 10 frames/s in a z-stack which 
was good enough for me.
I can record with the full frame rate of the camera in micromanager so

I also tried the new 64bit version (which works fine btw.) but that did 
not change anything in terms of acquisition speed.

Any help is really appreciated!

Hi Monika,

On 2015-05-05 17:29, m.pawlowska at nencki.gov.pl wrote:
> W dniu 2015-05-05 14:03, Johannes Schindelin napisa(a):
> 
>>> if I want to get OpenSPIM through fiji update site, I also need to
>>> activate the MicroManager-dev update site, or will it be installed
>>> automatically as a dependency of OpenSPIM?
>> 
>> It will be added automatically when you restart after activating the
>> OpenSPIM update site.
> 
> And what version of Micro-Manager will be downloaded? The last
> release, the nightly build, or something else?

The Micro-Manager-dev update site is populated automatically by the 
nightly build (read: by Micro-Manager's very own Jenkins job).

> I'm confused, because in the "About MicroManager" it says "MM Studio 
> version: 1.4.22 20150430, MMCore version 7.0.2" (I updated today) while 
> on the Micro-Manager website it says "Download Micro-Manager Latest 
> Release, Micro-Manager 1.4.21 (April 30, 2015) ". Yet the newest 
> nightly build is from May 4th.

Yeah, 1.4.22 is definitely wrong, most likely a typo (or preparing for 
the next release which is due July 31st).

The version you have as per the Micro-Manager-dev update site would be 
most appropriately described as 1.4.22-SNAPSHOT, i.e. a volatile version 
leading up to 1.4.22.

> I'm asking because I'm having issues with Micromanager, more precisely
> with Tools->Pixel Size Calibration, and I'm wondering whether going to
> an older or newer version would remove them.

The Micro-Manager developers are extremely helpful and nice, and they 
are very responsive (but keep in mind that they are in a different time 
zone: San Francisco, i.e. 9 hours behind us). I would suggest to write a 
mail to micro-manager-general at lists.sourceforge.net that describes the 
problem precisely -- ideally in such a manner that it is easy for any 
reader to reproduce the problem quickly. In my experience, most such bug 
descriptions on the mailing list are addressed swiftly.

Ciao,
Johannes

Hi All and especially Pete,

My setup is Orca R2, Coherent Cube, Picard stage.
I tested a couple of things and it it still unclear to me where the time 
is wasted.

I attached the core log of a 10 frame long time series (100ms exposure) 
recorded to memory with X/Y/Z Stage/Theta all unchecked and  without 
"Update Live preview".

I tried two configurations:
1. Orca  + Cube + Picard
2. Orca  + Picard

"1" took 7.6 s of which ("1"- "2") = 1.4 s are communication with laser, 
which, while way too much, is not the source of the problem.

Profiler("performAcquisition")[4 children]: 7.6113s
0.0017%:    Profiler("Output")[0 children]: 0.0001s
0.0000%:    Profiler("Acquisition")[0 children]: 0.0000s
24.0133%:    Profiler("Movement")[0 children]: 1.8277s
0.0013%:    Profiler("Setup")[0 children]: 0.0001s

So most of the time the system is doing something that the Profiler is 
not recording.

Looking at the core log I am a bit puzzled why the laser power is 
queried once  per slice and why the stage is told to move to the very 
position it currently is even though none of the motors should move at 
all since X/Y/Z/Theta are all unchecked in the acquisition dialog.

I would really appreciate any hint/suggestion on how to get back to 
reasonable acquisition speeds.

Thanks again!

Robert

> Hi All and especially Pete,
> 
> My setup is Orca R2, Coherent Cube, Picard stage.
> I tested a couple of things and it it still unclear to me where the 
> time
> is wasted.
> 
> I attached the core log of a 10 frame long time series (100ms exposure)
> recorded to memory with X/Y/Z Stage/Theta all unchecked and  without
> "Update Live preview".
> 
> I tried two configurations:
> 1. Orca  + Cube + Picard
> 2. Orca  + Picard
> 
> "1" took 7.6 s of which ("1"- "2") = 1.4 s are communication with 
> laser,
> which, while way too much, is not the source of the problem.
> 
> Profiler("performAcquisition")[4 children]: 7.6113s
> 0.0017%:    Profiler("Output")[0 children]: 0.0001s
> 0.0000%:    Profiler("Acquisition")[0 children]: 0.0000s
> 24.0133%:    Profiler("Movement")[0 children]: 1.8277s
> 0.0013%:    Profiler("Setup")[0 children]: 0.0001s
> 
> So most of the time the system is doing something that the Profiler is
> not recording.
> 
> Looking at the core log I am a bit puzzled why the laser power is
> queried once  per slice and why the stage is told to move to the very
> position it currently is even though none of the motors should move at
> all since X/Y/Z/Theta are all unchecked in the acquisition dialog.
> 
> I would really appreciate any hint/suggestion on how to get back to
> reasonable acquisition speeds.
> 
> Thanks again!
> 
> Robert

From johannes.schindelin at gmx.de  Fri May  8 05:31:24 2015
From: johannes.schindelin at gmx.de (Johannes Schindelin)
Date: Fri, 08 May 2015 12:31:24 +0200
Subject: [OpenSPIM] New Micro-Manager API: Home()
In-Reply-To: <d551ed95dc93c8e98d53d560336b288e@nencki.gov.pl>
References: <mailman.4303.1430923337.3596.openspim@openspim.org>
	<d551ed95dc93c8e98d53d560336b288e@nencki.gov.pl>
Message-ID: <93acf586b841b29c1d261c4d55bb95e8@www.dscho.org>

Hi Monika,

On 2015-05-07 19:11, m.pawlowska at nencki.gov.pl wrote:
> I tried to do it, just to see whether I can, but I can't and I feel
> that again the problem is not having sufficient information :/ How can
> I find out how this "SVN r15408" relates to the version available via
> Micro-Manager-Dev update site?

Unfortunately, it is not recorded. However, you can see the original 
Subversion revision (which the "SVN r15408" is referring to) in the 
commit message of our Git mirror, on the bottom of the commit messages. 
For example, r15408 corresponds to 
https://github.com/openspim/micromanager/commit/c46cd66d43e7fd55045ee690e281833dc0583d99 
which was committed on Tuesday, May 5th, so it should be in the nightly 
build as of Wednesday, May 6th (and as a consequence on the 
Micro-Manager-dev update site the same day, or at least one day later).

> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.194887 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Will home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.208887 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Did home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.208887 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Will home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.224888 tid5692 [dbg,Core] Did home xy stage Picard 
> XY Stage
> 2015-05-07T18:49:23.224888 tid5692 [IFO,App] Could not home Z stage.
>                                    [       ] java.lang.Exception:
> Device "Picard Z Stage" is of the wrong type for the requested
> operation in Thread[AWT-EventQueue-0,6,main]

It appears that this error message comes from 
https://github.com/openspim/micromanager/blob/f88b6b5ff341061d777511e33c7291a3d498d431/MMCore/DeviceManager.h#L97 
(I called `git grep "of the wrong type"` to find out).

The commit you referenced replaced the `GetDeviceOfType()` call in 
`MMCore::home()` with a `GetDevice()` call: 
https://github.com/openspim/micromanager/commit/c46cd66d43e7fd55045ee690e281833dc0583d99#diff-66e4d1b12dce965612b0d94db6c9f1d6R1619 
-- therefore I think that this line:

>                                    [       ]   at
> mmcorej.MMCoreJJNI.CMMCore_home(Native Method)

hints at outdated Micro-Manager binaries. Having said that, it appears 
as if the Micro-Manager-dev update site has not been updated in a couple 
of days: http://sites.imagej.net/Micro-Manager-dev/mm/win64/?C=M;O=D

I have to run right now, but will investigate more later.

Thank you,
Johannes

From johannes.schindelin at gmx.de  Wed May 13 04:17:30 2015
From: johannes.schindelin at gmx.de (Johannes Schindelin)
Date: Wed, 13 May 2015 11:17:30 +0200
Subject: [OpenSPIM] very slow acquisition speed
In-Reply-To: <5551F4F5.3050403@ist.ac.at>
References: <mailman.4342.1431012438.3596.openspim@openspim.org>
	<b25a1860360928b2fc54bbc7721b4dde@nencki.gov.pl>
	<5551F4F5.3050403@ist.ac.at>
Message-ID: <a858dafc1c8aae2d5342914d10a57181@www.dscho.org>

Hi Robert,

On 2015-05-12 14:41, Robert Hauschild wrote:

> Would be great if someone could tell me how to figure out what is
> going on during the 75% of time that is unaccounted for in the
> profiler!

The profiler (which one are you using? That information is missing from 
the original report) can only profile Java code, not native code. So my 
guess is that something wonky is going on in the C++ part. 
Alternatively, it could be that the code is just waiting for the motors 
to arrive at the desired position, which would also not be recorded by 
the profiler.

Personally, I would try to go for the Flight Recorder of Java Mission 
Control: http://fiji.sc/Profiling_Java_Code#Java_Mission_Control. There 
is an Eclipse plugin with which you can toggle the flight recording more 
precisely; It is not described in the Fiji wiki because neither I nor 
anybody else found the time to describe it there, but there are links on 
Oracle's site: 
http://www.oracle.com/technetwork/java/javaseproducts/mission-control/index.html

Ciao,
Johannes

From johannes.schindelin at gmx.de  Wed May 13 04:59:00 2015

Subject: [OpenSPIM] 64-bit Fiji Memory Limit Issue
In-Reply-To: <1431353493456.12540@ucl.ac.uk>

	<1431353493456.12540@ucl.ac.uk>
Message-ID: <a88c576f3ff07f4d01e577487451809b@www.dscho.org>

Dear Thomas,

please note that while it is convenient for you to take this problem to 
a private mail exchange with me, it is really inconvenient for me: I 
have nothing to gain from a private mail exchange solving this issue -- 
it is taking my time, to solve a problem that is not mine, in a plugin 
that is not mine, and the warm and fuzzy feeling of solving a single 
problem for a single person when nobody else knows what I managed to 
accomplish does not further my career nor does it pay my bills -- while 
a public discussion not only offers the possibility that other people 
than you might benefit from my advice (which would in turn help me), but 
also offers the possibility that other people might help you, relieving 
me.

I really wish that more people were trying to help the OpenSPIM 
community thrive as a publicly visible community. There are some 
laudable examples on the OpenSPIM mailing list recently, and I am very 
thankful for that.

On 2015-05-11 16:11, Roberts, Thomas wrote:

> I am still encountering this memory issue, unfortunately.
> 
> I downloaded the latest version of the OpenSPIM software that you sent
> a link to a few weeks ago
> (http://openspim.org/downloads/OpenSPIM-20150427.zip).

Please note that it is not obvious from your screenshots what amount of 
memory Fiji *actually* reserves. Two Fiji instances running side by 
side, for example, will not have the same amount of memory available 
because Java works by reserving the memory at start-up, and that memory 
is then not available to a second Fiji instance. The ImageJ launcher 
will detect that less memory is available than it was asked to ask for 
and fall back to try with a lesser amount. That is my guess regarding 
what happens on your computer.

By clicking on the status bar, you will see how much memory Fiji's Java 
VM thinks is available. Clicking on the status bar will also trigger a 
so-called "garbage collection", i.e. it will ask the Java VM to 
re-organize its memory consumption. Therefore, sporadically clicking on 
the status bar while the plugin is running might even work around the 
memory issue.

> However, I still can't open large images in Fiji. I am trying to run
> through the Bead Based Registration tutorial on OpenSPIM.org, but I
> encounter the Memory Limit issue - I've attached some PNGs showing the
> error messages.
> 
> I tried your suggestion of opening the memory monitor, but it doesn't
> really tell me much - just that the program spikes and stops once it
> reaches the 494MB memory limit (see image1.png).
> 
> I still don't understand why Fiji thinks it has 5000MB of memory
> available, but crashes at 500MB (see image2.png).

You really scared me when you said that it crashed. You see, "to crash" 
means one very specific thing, and that thing only, when you talk about 
computer programs: it means that the entire application just stopped to 
run, all its windows vanished, without any error message nor a chance to 
store so-far unsaved data.

That is distinctly not what happened. What you saw is an 
OutOfMemoryException which stopped the plugin but nothing else.

> Also, I have tried running the registration tutorial on my office
> computer, and this works, but the machine is very slow for such large
> datasets.

It might make sense to open large images in that Fiji instance first, 
until it runs out of memory, in order to determine whether the problem 
lies with the Java VM in general, or with the plugin you are trying to 
run. I am getting the impression that something is wrong with your Fiji 
installation rather than with the SPIM Registration plugin.

Ciao,
Johannes

Hi Monika,

On Wed, May 13, 2015 at 09:38:21AM -0700, Chris Weisiger wrote:
> On Wed, May 13, 2015 at 9:15 AM, <m.pawlowska at nencki.gov.pl> wrote:
> > W dniu 2015-05-13 17:52, Chris Weisiger napisa(a):
> > indeed, with the newest nightly build the acquisition works. But this
> > solves my problem only partly. I am normally using fiji with  
> Micromanager
> > update site, and from there the newest build is the 20150430, this is  
> why
> > I'm using this version. I would prefer to use fiji to have all the
> > aditional functionality. Is there any chance to get the update site
> > updated, so to say?
>
> Okay, good to know we've at least narrowed down what's going on. In this
> case I suspect the actual problem isn't the version of Micro-Manager, but
> the version of the OME library in Fiji. Sometimes Micro-Manager and Fiji
> depend on the same library, but require different versions of that  
> library,
> which is unfortunate; we're trying to resolve such issues when we  
> discover
> them.
>
> In the meantime, you can try replacing the library manually. This is a  
> jar
> file called "ome-xml.jar", which should be in the "plugins/Micro-Manager"
> directory of the nightly download. You can try just replacing the
> corresponding .jar file in your Fiji installation with the one from the
> nightly build. Make a backup of the original .jar file though, just in  
> case
> something else in Fiji breaks. In the meantime, we can look into what it
> would take to get the update site updated.

The conflict is in other JARs. We still use an outdated version of
scifio.jar, which conflicts with the newer version in Fiji. We fully
intend to fix this, and it will hopefully not be too hard, but it is not
trivial (we need to make sure we don't introduce issues into file saving
in our official release, and that will require careful testing).

Please consider the Micro-Manager-dev update site to be experimental.

I don't think there is an easy fix at this moment that can be done by
just replacing JARs. We'll keep working on it!

Best,
Mark

I have discovered a problem with micromanager 1.4.22 and the Orca ER. When I take a z-stack the resulting images are split. The left 1/3 of the image is fused to the right 2/3. The problem has something to to do with the Picard stage as taking 10 images quickly without stage movement results in intact images. Taking images of multiple xy positions results in split images. I replaced the Orca ER and associated control box with another Orca ER setup and the problem persisted.  I reinstalled an earlier version of micromanager (1.4.19) and the problem went away. Are earlier versions of Openspim software archived somewhere? I would like to download a version with mm 1.4.19.

At the time we were using a Hamamatsu Orca ER, which is firewire based, hence the need for a computer with a firewire port. A portable laptop computer is a nice thing to have, but not necessary.

From fredrik.ek at med.lu.se  Tue May 26 01:24:52 2015
From: fredrik.ek at med.lu.se (Fredrik Ek)
Date: Tue, 26 May 2015 06:24:52 +0000
Subject: [OpenSPIM] multiline openSPIM with Lighthub-4
In-Reply-To: <55636591.6040901@cc.huji.ac.il>
References: <555AFFD5.9010106@cc.huji.ac.il>
	<180212231.32691920.1432027731107.JavaMail.zimbra@mpi-cbg.de>
	<555B0B70.9090300@cc.huji.ac.il> <55636591.6040901@cc.huji.ac.il>
Message-ID: <11FEABF97C42FE47AA23C843A13D49EEEDB2839A@UWMBX04.uw.lu.se>

Hi Aryeh,

We have just recently finished the build of a dual side illumination system using the lighthub-6 with 3 laser lines. I will upload pictures and details within next coming weeks on the wiki page. The first point is to go for the lighthub-6 since the price difference is very small. This will allow an expansion in the future with more lasers. The fiber is coupled to a fiber collimator fixed to a holder on a rail to allow for alignment with the beam splitter. Today I would have built it with a small xz stage for improved alignment or at least a sturdier holder of the collimator. There are some examples at Thorlabs. I have added the links to the details that we used in the current setup. It is important to get a good fixation of the collimator especially if you like to use the laser module in other microscopes and regularly shifts the fiber. 

I hope this will help you!

collimator http://www.thorlabs.de/thorproduct.cfm?partnumber=F240APC-A
adaptor http://www.thorlabs.de/thorproduct.cfm?partnumber=AD12NT
Holder http://www.thorlabs.de/thorproduct.cfm?partnumber=FMP1

BR

Fredrik

From winfrees at iu.edu  Tue May 26 11:04:41 2015
From: winfrees at iu.edu (Winfree, Seth)
Date: Tue, 26 May 2015 16:04:41 +0000
Subject: [OpenSPIM] perfusion and multiple lasers
Message-ID: <0BB84AC4E46D2D4AB1AE4C111324E8D63E390C96@IU-MSSG-MBX107.ads.iu.edu>

SPIMers,

We have completed a multichannel AOTF modulated 4 line L-SPIM.  We took an AOTF and three retired lasers(442,488,514,568,647) from our spinning disk and designed a DAC based on the Arduino DAC supported by micromanager (the 442 is not quite integrated optically).  We've also incorporated an emission filter wheel and excitation wheel for beam characterizing (the former is integrated in our branch of the SPIMAcquisition plugin).  I plan to have the optics/hardware/software design and example datasets up on the OpenSPIM site in the coming weeks-grant taking precedent.  I'm working with Johannes to get our branch of SPIMAcquisition merged with the release version-waiting on me really.

On the perfusion and environmental control side, we have a summer student that is working on these aspects for our system.  The perfusion is going to be fairly rudimentary.  We will be relying on peristaltic pumps because the volume of our sample chamber is so large (7 ml).  The perfusion system will be setup to work as a recirculating loop as well to deliver dissolved gases CO2 etc as required-via a simple bubbler.  If I can find a CO2 sensor I like(cost to performance) this might be integrated into the bubbler unit.

I'm not crazy about directly heating the chamber with amped up resistors, so we're starting with a "closed-loop" heated reservoir, re-circulator and heat-exchanger-if it works well we may also strap a Peltier based heat pump to the reservoir as well to give us cooling.

In toto there will be a handful of peristaltic pumps, controllers (Arduino as PIDs), media bubblers and heated reservoirs.  As time permits we'll be writing a plugin for micromanager to wrangle all this functionality and add graphs etc-everything you might want out of a comparable Peco or Okolabs solution.

As we make progress I'll update our  to-be-completed OpenSPIM page.
Happy SPIMing!

Seth

From weber at mpi-cbg.de  Wed May 27 10:41:22 2015
From: weber at mpi-cbg.de (Michael Weber)
Date: Wed, 27 May 2015 17:41:22 +0200
Subject: [OpenSPIM] sCMOS global vs rolling shutter
In-Reply-To: <5564744D.4000408@cc.huji.ac.il>
References: <555AFFD5.9010106@cc.huji.ac.il>	<180212231.32691920.1432027731107.JavaMail.zimbra@mpi-cbg.de>	<555B0B70.9090300@cc.huji.ac.il>
	<55636591.6040901@cc.huji.ac.il>
	<11FEABF97C42FE47AA23C843A13D49EEEDB2839A@UWMBX04.uw.lu.se>
	<5564744D.4000408@cc.huji.ac.il>
Message-ID: <BA71BC0A-3573-4ACB-9F0B-235CF40EBA13@mpi-cbg.de>

Dear Aryeh,

rolling shutter gives you twice the speed, but potential artifacts caused by the time offset across the frame. There are cameras which give you both shutter modes (Andor Zyla etc.), if you are willing to give up some QE. It really depends on your specimen, and what kind of analysis you want to do. Unless you want to quantify rapid movements across the frame (e.g. fast fluidics), I would say rolling shutter is fine.

Best,
Michael
